\\n419: // QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"QueueSort\\\" plugins.\\n420: // These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\\n421: // plugin may be enabled at a time.\\n422: type QueueSortPlugin interface {\\n423: \\tPlugin\\n424: \\t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\\n425: \\tLess(QueuedPodInfo, QueuedPodInfo) bool\\n426: }\\n427: \\n428: // EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\\n429: // move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\\n430: // In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\\n431: // and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\\n432: // Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\\n433: // and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\\n434: // This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\\n435: // and we have no choose but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\\n436: //\\n437: // Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) must implement this interface,\\n438: // otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\\n439: //\\n440: // Also, if EventsToRegister returns an empty list, that means the Pods failed by the plugin are not requeued by any events,\\n441: // which doesn't make sense in most cases (very likely misuse)\\n442: // since the pods rejected by the plugin could be stuck in the unschedulable pod pool forever.\\n443: //\\n444: // If plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\\n445: type EnqueueExtensions interface {\\n446: \\tPlugin\\n447: \\t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\\n448: \\t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\\n449: \\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\n450: \\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\\n451: \\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\\n452: \\t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\\n453: \\t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\\n454: \\t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\\n455: \\t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\\n456: \\t//\\n457: \\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\\n458: \\tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\\n459: }\\n460: \\n461: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\\n462: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\\n463: // state.\\n464: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\\n465: \\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n466: \\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n467: \\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd PodInfo, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\\n468: \\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n469: \\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n470: \\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove PodInfo, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\\n471: }\\n472: \\n473: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreFilter\\\" plugins.\\n474: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. Plugins that implement PreFilterPlugin should\\n475: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\\n476: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\\n477: \\tPlugin\\n478: \\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\\n479: \\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\\n480: \\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. Plugins that implement FilterPlugin should\\n504: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\\n505: type FilterPlugin interface {\\n506: \\tPlugin\\n507: \\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\\n508: \\t// All FilterPlugins should return \\\"Success\\\" to declare that\\n509: \\t// the given node fits the pod. These plugins are called\\n533: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\\n534: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\\n535: \\tPlugin\\n536: \\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\\n537: \\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n538: \\t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\\n539: \\t//\\n540: \\t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\\n541: \\t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n542: \\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n543: \\t//\\n544: \\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\\n545: \\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\\n546: \\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\\n547: \\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\\n548: \\t//\\n549: \\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\\n550: \\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. A permit plugin\\n647: \\t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\\n648: \\t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\\n649: \\t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \\\"wait\\\", the framework will wait only\\n650: \\t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\\n651: \\tPermit(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\\n652: }\\n653: \\n654: // BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"Bind\\\" plugins. Bind\\n655: // plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\\n656: type BindPlugin interface {\\n657: \\tPlugin\\n658: \\t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\\n659: \\t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\\n660: \\t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin chooses to handle a Pod, the\\n661: \\t// remaining bind plugins are skipped. When a bind plugin does not handle a pod,\\n662: \\t// it must return Skip in its Status code. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\\n663: \\t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\\n664: \\tBind(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n665: }\\n666: \\n667: // A portion of a pod signature. The sign fragments from all plugins are combined\\n668: // together to create a unified signature.\\n669: type SignFragment struct {\\n670: \\t// Pod signature fragments are identified by a key, i.e., fragments with the same key\\n671: \\t// should contain the same value for the same pod. Plugin authors can return the same SignFragment\\n672: \\t// from multiple plugins, the framework just ignores duplicates. This allows plugins to share signers easily.\\n673: \\t//\\n674: \\t// Fragment names can be found in k8s.io/kube-scheduler/framework/signers.go. New fragment names for\\n675: \\t// in-tree plugins should be added there, and custom plugins can also use them.\\n676: \\t// Simple SignFragments which return a field should have names that follow the field name they return.\\n677: \\t// So a SignFragment that returns NodeName would have the key:\\n678: \\t//\\n679: \\t//\\t\\\"v1.Pod.Spec.NodeName\\\"\\n680: \\t//\\n681: \\t// If a SignFragment does some processing on the resource, its name should include the path to the base of the state it uses,\\n682: \\t// and then suffix this with a descriptive function name followed by (). So, for example, a SignFragment that only returns\\n683: \\t// Ephemeral volumes might use the key:\\n684: \\t//\\n685: \\t//\\t\\\"v1.Pod.Volumes.EphemeralVolumes()\\\"\\n686: \\tKey string\\n687: \\n688: \\t// The value of a SignFragment must be a json-marshallable object. Remember that we need to compare these across pods, so\\n689: \\t// plugins should ensure that lists where order doesn't matter are sorted, for example.\\n690: \\tValue any\\n691: }\\n692: \\n693: // The signature for a given pod after all of the results from plugins are consolidated.\\n694: type PodSignature []byte\\n695: \\n696: // SignPlugin is an interface that should be implemented by plugins that either filter or score\\n697: // pods to enable batching and gang scheduling optimizations.\\n698: // Each plugin returns SignFragments used to build a single signature per pod entering the scheduling cycle,\\n699: // and the scheduler uses signatures to determine whether it can use a cached scheduling result, or needs to\\n700: // recompute the prioritized nodes.\\n701: //\\n702: // If an enabled plugin that does Scoring, Prescoring, Filtering or Prefiltering does not implement this interface we will turn off batching for all pods.\\n703: type SignPlugin interface {\\n704: \\tPlugin\\n705: \\t// SignPod returns SignFragments for use in batching. This is called at every scheduling cycle\\n706: \\t// and is used to construct a signature builder used for pods. (KEP-5598).\\n707: \\t//\\n708: \\t// The sign fragments from all the plugins are combined to create a single signature. Only one fragment\\n709: \\t// with a given key will be included.\\n710: \\t//\\n711: \\t// Status means:\\n712: \\t//   - Success: the signer can sign the pod, accompanied by a set of signature fragments to be included.\\n713: \\t//   - Unschedulable: the signer refuses to sign the pod, meaning the pod is not eligible for opportunistic batching optimization.\\n714: \\t//   - Error: the signer hits something _unexpected_ and cannot build sign(s). A framework runtime just\\n715: \\t//     proceeds with scheduling this pod without opportunistic batching optimization like Unschedulable,\\n716: \\t//     but just report errors to logs.\\n717: \\tSignPod(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod) ([]SignFragment, *Status)\\n718: }\\n719: \\n720: // Handle provides data and some tools that plugins can use. It is\\n721: // passed to the plugin factories at the time of plugin initialization. Plugins\\n722: // must store and use this handle to call framework functions.\\n723: type Handle interface {\\n724: \\t// PodNominator abstracts operations to maintain nominated Pods.\\n725: \\tPodNominator\\n726: \\t// PluginsRunner abstracts operations to run some plugins.\\n727: \\tPluginsRunner\\n728: \\t// PodActivator abstracts operations in the scheduling queue.\\n729: \\tPodActivator\\n730: \\t// SnapshotSharedLister returns listers from the latest NodeInfo Snapshot. cycle (pre-bind/bind/post-bind/un-reserve plugin)\\n737: \\t//   otherwise, a concurrent read/write error might occur.\\n738: \\t// - There is no guarantee that the information is always up-to-date.\\n739: \\t//   So, plugins shouldn't use it in QueueingHint and PreEnqueue\\n740: \\t//   otherwise, they might make a decision based on stale information.\\n741: \\t//\\n742: \\t// (\\n22: \\t\\\"context\\\"\\n23: \\t\\\"errors\\\"\\n24: \\t\\\"math\\\"\\n25: \\t\\\"strings\\\"\\n26: \\t\\\"time\\\"\\n27: \\n28: \\t\\\"github.com/google/go-cmp/cmp\\\"         //nolint:depguard\\n29: \\t\\\"github.com/google/go-cmp/cmp/cmpopts\\\" //nolint:depguard\\n30: \\tv1 \\\"k8s.io/api/core/v1\\\"\\n31: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/types\\\"\\n32: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/sets\\\"\\n33: \\t\\\"k8s.io/client-go/informers\\\"\\n34: \\tclientset \\\"k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes\\\"\\n35: \\trestclient \\\"k8s.io/client-go/rest\\\"\\n36: \\t\\\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/events\\\"\\n37: \\t\\\"k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue\\\"\\n38: \\t\\\"k8s.io/klog/v2\\\"\\n39: )\\n40: \\n41: // Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\\n42: type Code int\\n43: \\n44: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\\n45: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\\n46: const (\\n47: \\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\\n48: \\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \\\"Success\\\".\\n49: \\tSuccess Code = iota\\n50: \\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\\n51: \\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\\n52: \\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\\n53: \\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\\n54: \\tError\\n55: \\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\\n56: \\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\\n57: \\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\\n58: \\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\\n59: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n60: \\t//\\n61: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n62: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\\n63: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n64: \\tUnschedulable\\n65: \\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\\n66: \\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\\n67: \\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\\n68: \\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\\n69: \\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\\n70: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n71: \\t//\\n72: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n73: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\\n74: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n75: \\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n76: \\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\\n77: \\tWait\\n78: \\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\\n79: \\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\\n80: \\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\\n81: \\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\\n82: \\tSkip\\n83: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n84: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n85: \\t//\\n86: \\t// For example, if your plugin has to notify the scheduling result to an external component,\\n87: \\t// and wait for it to complete something **before** binding.\\n88: \\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\\n89: \\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\\n90: \\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\\n91: \\t//\\n92: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n93: \\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\\n94: \\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\\n95: \\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\\n96: \\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\\n97: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\\n98: \\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\\n99: \\tPending\\n100: )\\n101: \\n102: // This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\\n103: var codes = []string{\\\"Success\\\", \\\"Error\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\", \\\"Wait\\\", \\\"Skip\\\", \\\"Pending\\\"}\\n104: \\n105: func (c Code) String() string {\\n106: \\treturn codes[c]\\n107: }\\n108: \\n109: // Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\\n110: // message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\\n111: // When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\\n112: // And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\\n113: // NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\\n114: type Status struct {\\n115: \\tcode    Code\\n116: \\treasons []string\\n117: \\terr     error\\n118: \\t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\\n119: \\t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\\n120: \\tplugin string\\n121: }\\n122: \\n123: func (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\\n124: \\ts.err = err\\n125: \\treturn s\\n126: }\\n127: \\n128: // Code returns code of the Status.\\n129: func (s *Status) Code() Code {\\n130: \\tif s == nil {\\n131: \\t\\treturn Success\\n132: \\t}\\n133: \\treturn s.code\\n134: }\\n135: \\n136: // }\\n148: \\n149: // WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\\n150: // and returns the given status object.\\n151: func (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\\n152: \\ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\\n153: \\treturn s\\n154: }\\n155: \\n156: // Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\\n157: func (s *Status) Plugin() string {\\n158: \\treturn s.plugin\\n159: }\\n160: \\n161: // Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\\n162: func (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\\n163: \\tif s.err != nil {\\n164: \\t\\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, \\ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\\n172: }\\n173: \\n174: // IsSuccess returns true if and only if \\\"Status\\\" is nil or Code is \\\"Success\\\".\\n175: func (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool }\\n206: \\n207: // Equal checks equality of two statuses. \\tPreEnqueue(ctx context.Context, p *v1.Pod) *Status\\n414: }\\n415: \\n416: // LessFunc is the function to sort pod info\\n417: type LessFunc func(podInfo1, podInfo2 QueuedPodInfo) bool\\n418: \\n419: // QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"QueueSort\\\" plugins.\\n420: // These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\\n421: // plugin may be enabled at a time.\\n422: type QueueSortPlugin interface {\\n423: \\tPlugin\\n424: \\t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\\n425: \\tLess(QueuedPodInfo, QueuedPodInfo) bool\\n426: }\\n427: \\n428: // EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\\n429: // move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\\n430: // In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\\n431: // and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\\n432: // Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\\n433: // and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\\n434: // This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\\n435: // and we have no choose but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\\n436: //\\n437: // Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) must implement this interface,\\n438: // otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\\n439: //\\n440: // Also, if EventsToRegister returns an empty list, that means the Pods failed by the plugin are not requeued by any events,\\n441: // which doesn't make sense in most cases (very likely misuse)\\n442: // since the pods rejected by the plugin could be stuck in the unschedulable pod pool forever.\\n443: //\\n444: // If plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\\n445: type EnqueueExtensions interface {\\n446: \\tPlugin\\n447: \\t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\\n448: \\t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\\n449: \\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\n450: \\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\\n451: \\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\\n452: \\t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\\n453: \\t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\\n454: \\t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\\n455: \\t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\\n456: \\t//\\n457: \\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\\n458: \\tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\\n459: }\\n460: \\n461: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\\n462: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\\n463: // state.\\n464: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\\n465: \\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n466: \\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n467: \\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd PodInfo, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\\n468: \\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n469: \\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n470: \\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove PodInfo, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\\n471: }\\n472: \\n473: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreFilter\\\" plugins.\\n474: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. Plugins that implement PreFilterPlugin should\\n475: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\\n476: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\\n477: \\tPlugin\\n478: \\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\\n479: \\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\\n480: \\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\\n481: \\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\\n482: \\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\".\\n483: \\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\\n484: \\t//\\n485: \\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\\n486: \\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\\n487: \\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodes []NodeInfo) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\\n488: \\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\\n489: \\t// or nil if it does not. These plugins are called at the\\n498: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\\n499: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\\n500: // These plugins should return \\\"Success\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\" in Status.code.\\n501: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\\n502: // Anything other than \\\"Success\\\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\\n503: // running the pod. Plugins that implement FilterPlugin should\\n504: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\\n505: type FilterPlugin interface {\\n506: \\tPlugin\\n507: \\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\\n508: \\t// All FilterPlugins should return \\\"Success\\\" to declare that\\n509: \\t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n510: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n511: \\t//\\n512: \\t// \\\"Error\\\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\\n513: \\t//\\n514: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n515: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n516: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n517: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n518: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n519: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n520: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n521: \\t//\\n522: \\t// Plugins are encouraged to check the context for cancellation.\\n523: \\t// Once canceled, they should return as soon as possible with\\n524: \\t// an UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status that includes the\\n525: \\t// `context.Cause(ctx)` error explanation. For example, the\\n526: \\t// context gets canceled when a sufficient number of suitable\\n527: \\t// nodes have been found and searching for more isn't necessary\\n528: \\t// anymore.\\n529: \\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\\n530: }\\n531: \\n532: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \\\"PostFilter\\\" plugins. These plugins are called\\n533: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\\n534: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\\n535: \\tPlugin\\n536: \\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\\n537: \\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n538: \\t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\\n539: \\t//\\n540: \\t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\\n541: \\t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n542: \\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n543: \\t//\\n544: \\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\\n545: \\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\\n546: \\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\\n547: \\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\\n548: \\t//\\n549: \\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\\n550: \\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. Plugin authors can return the same SignFragment\\n672: \\t// from multiple plugins, the framework just ignores duplicates. This allows plugins to share signers easily.\\n673: \\t//\\n674: \\t// Fragment names can be found in k8s.io/kube-scheduler/framework/signers.go. Max number of chunks is param pieces.\\n814: \\tUntil(ctx context.Context, pieces int, doWorkPiece workqueue.DoWorkPieceFunc, operation string)\\n815: }\\n816: \\n817: // PodActivator abstracts operations in the scheduling queue.\\n818: type PodActivator interface {\\n819: \\t// Activate moves the given pods to activeQ.\\n820: \\t// If a pod isn't found in unschedulablePods or backoffQ and it's in-flight,\\n821: \\t// the wildcard event is registered so that the pod will be requeued when it comes back.\\n822: \\t// But, if a pod isn't found in unschedulablePods or backoffQ and it's not in-flight (i.e., completely unknown pod),\\n823: \\t// Activate would ignore the pod.\\n824: \\tActivate(logger klog.Logger, pods map[string]*v1.Pod)\\n825: }\\n826: \\n827: // PodNominator abstracts operations to maintain nominated Pods.\\n828: type PodNominator interface {\\n829: \\t// AddNominatedPod adds the given pod to the nominator or\\n830: \\t// updates it if it already exists.\\n831: \\tAddNominatedPod(logger klog.Logger, pod PodInfo, nominatingInfo *NominatingInfo)\\n832: \\t// DeleteNominatedPodIfExists deletes nominatedPod from internal cache. If any\\n845: \\t// of these plugins returns any status other than \\\"Success\\\", the given pod is rejected.\\n846: \\tRunPreScorePlugins(context.Context, CycleState, *v1.Pod, []NodeInfo) *Status\\n847: \\t// RunScorePlugins runs the set of configured scoring plugins.\\n848: \\t// It returns a list that stores scores from each plugin and total score for each Node.\\n849: \\t// It also returns *Status, which is set to non-success if any of the plugins returns\\n850: \\t// a non-success status.\\n851: \\tRunScorePlugins(context.Context, CycleState, *v1.Pod, []NodeInfo) ([]NodePluginScores, *Status)\\n852: \\t// RunFilterPlugins runs the set of configured Filter plugins for pod on\\n853: \\t// the given node. \n41: // Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\n42: type Code int\n43: \n44: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\n45: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\n46: const (\n47: \t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\n48: \t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \"Success\".\n49: \tSuccess Code = iota\n50: \t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\n51: \t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\n52: \t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\n53: \t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\n54: \tError\n55: \t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n56: \t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n57: \t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n58: \t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n59: \t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n60: \t//\n61: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n62: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n63: \t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n64: \tUnschedulable\n65: \t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n66: \t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n67: \t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n68: \t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n69: \t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n70: \t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n71: \t//\n72: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n73: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n74: \t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n75: \tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n76: \t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n77: \tWait\n78: \t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n79: \t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n80: \t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n81: \t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n82: \tSkip\n83: \t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n84: \t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n85: \t//\n86: \t// For example, if your plugin has to notify the scheduling result to an external component,\n87: \t// and wait for it to complete something **before** binding.\n88: \t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n89: \t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n90: \t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n91: \t//\n92: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n93: \t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n94: \t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n95: \t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n96: \t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n97: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\n98: \t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\n99: \tPending\n100: )\n101: \n102: // This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\n103: var codes = []string{\"Success\", \"Error\", \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\", \"Wait\", \"Skip\", \"Pending\"}\n104: \n105: func (c Code) String() string {\n106: \treturn codes[c]\n107: }\n108: \n109: // Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\n110: // message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\n111: // When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\n112: // And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\n113: // NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\n114: type Status struct {\n115: \tcode    Code\n116: \treasons []string\n117: \terr     error\n118: \t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\n119: \t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\n120: \tplugin string\n121: }\n122: \n123: func (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\n124: \ts.err = err\n125: \treturn s\n126: }\n127: \n128: // Code returns code of the Status.\n129: func (s *Status) Code() Code {\n130: \tif s == nil {\n131: \t\treturn Success\n132: \t}\n133: \treturn s.code\n134: }\n135: \n136: // Message returns a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\n137: func (s *Status) Message() string {\n138: \tif s == nil {\n139: \t\treturn \"\"\n140: \t}\n141: \treturn strings.Join(s.Reasons(), \", \")\n142: }\n143: \n144: // SetPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin.\n145: func (s *Status) SetPlugin(plugin string) {\n146: \ts.plugin = plugin\n147: }\n148: \n149: // WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\n150: // and returns the given status object.\n151: func (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\n152: \ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\n153: \treturn s\n154: }\n155: \n156: // Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\n157: func (s *Status) Plugin() string {\n158: \treturn s.plugin\n159: }\n160: \n161: // Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\n162: func (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\n163: \tif s.err != nil {\n164: \t\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, s.reasons...)\n165: \t}\n166: \treturn s.reasons\n167: }\n168: \n169: // AppendReason appends given reason to the Status.\n170: func (s *Status) AppendReason(reason string) {\n171: \ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\n172: }\n173: \n174: // IsSuccess returns true if and only if \"Status\" is nil or Code is \"Success\".\n175: func (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool {\n176: \treturn s.Code() == Success\n177: }\n178: \n179: // IsWait returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Wait\".\n180: func (s *Status) IsWait() bool {\n181: \treturn s.Code() == Wait\n182: }\n183: \n184: // IsSkip returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Skip\".\n185: func (s *Status) IsSkip() bool {\n186: \treturn s.Code() == Skip\n187: }\n188: \n189: // IsRejected returns true if \"Status\" is Unschedulable (Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, or Pending).\n190: func (s *Status) IsRejected() bool {\n191: \tcode := s.Code()\n192: \treturn code == Unschedulable || code == UnschedulableAndUnresolvable || code == Pending\n193: }\n194: \n195: // AsError returns nil if the status is a success, a wait or a skip; otherwise returns an \"error\" object\n196: // with a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\n197: func (s *Status) AsError() error {\n198: \tif s.IsSuccess() || s.IsWait() || s.IsSkip() {\n199: \t\treturn nil\n200: \t}\n201: \tif s.err != nil {\n202: \t\treturn s.err\n203: \t}\n204: \treturn errors.New(s.Message())\n205: }\n206: \n207: // Equal checks equality of two statuses. This is useful for testing with\n208: // cmp.Equal.\n209: func (s *Status) Equal(x *Status) bool {\n210: \tif s == nil || x == nil {\n211: \t\treturn s.IsSuccess() && x.IsSuccess()\n212: \t}\n213: \tif s.code != x.code {\n214: \t\treturn false\n215: \t}\n216: \tif !cmp.Equal(s.err, x.err, cmpopts.EquateErrors()) {\n217: \t\treturn false\n218: \t}\n219: \tif !cmp.Equal(s.reasons, x.reasons) {\n220: \t\treturn false\n221: \t}\n222: \treturn cmp.Equal(s.plugin, x.plugin)\n223: }\n224: \n225: func (s *Status) String() string {\n226: \treturn s.Message()\n227: }\n228: \n229: // NewStatus makes a Status out of the given arguments and returns its pointer.\n230: func NewStatus(code Code, reasons ...string) *Status {\n231: \ts := &Status{\n232: \t\tcode:    code,\n233: \t\treasons: reasons,\n234: \t}\n235: \treturn s\n236: }\n237: \n238: // AsStatus wraps an error in a Status.\n239: func AsStatus(err error) *Status {\n240: \tif err == nil {\n241: \t\treturn nil\n242: \t}\n243: \treturn &Status{\n244: \t\tcode: Error,\n245: \t\terr:  err,\n246: \t}\n247: }\n248: \n249: // NodeToStatusReader is a read-only interface of NodeToStatus passed to each PostFilter plugin.\n250: type \tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n297: )\n298: \n299: type NominatingMode int\n300: \n301: const (\n302: \tModeNoop NominatingMode = iota\n303: \tModeOverride\n304: )\n305: \n306: type pod currently in preBind phase.\n336: type PodInPreBind interface {\n337: \t// CancelPod cancels the context attached to a goroutine running binding cycle of this pod\n338: \t// if the pod is not cancel the context of binding cycle\n343: \t// via PodInPreBind\n344: \t// Returns false if the context was already canceled.\n345: \tMarkPrebound() bool\n346: }\n347: \n348: // PreFilterResult wraps needed info for scheduler framework to act upon PreFilter phase.\n349: type PreFilterResult struct {\n350: \t// The set of nodes that should be considered downstream; if nil then\n351: \t// all nodes are eligible.\n352: \tNodeNames sets.Set[string]\n353: }\n354: \n355: func (p *PreFilterResult) AllNodes() bool {\n356: \treturn p == nil || p.NodeNames == nil\n357: }\n358: \n359: func (p *PreFilterResult) Merge(in *PreFilterResult) *PreFilterResult {\n360: \tif p.AllNodes() && in.AllNodes() {\n361: \t\treturn nil\n362: \t}\n363: \n364: \tr := PreFilterResult{}\n365: \tif p.AllNodes() {\n366: \t\tr.NodeNames = in.NodeNames.Clone()\n367: \t\treturn &r\n368: \t}\n369: \tif in.AllNodes() {\n370: \t\tr.NodeNames = p.NodeNames.Clone()\n371: \t\treturn &r\n372: \t}\n373: \n374: \tr.NodeNames = p.NodeNames.Intersection(in.NodeNames)\n375: \treturn &r\n376: }\n377: \n378: // PostFilterResult wraps needed info for scheduler framework to act upon PostFilter phase.\n379: type group, this field skips the pods that were\n383: \t// identified as victims for other members of the pod group.\n384: \tVictims []*v1.Pod\n385: }\n386: \n387: // PreBindPreFlightResult wraps needed info for scheduler framework to act upon PreBindPreFlight phase.\n388: type PreBindPreFlightResult struct {\n389: \t// AllowParallel indicates whether this plugin's PreBind method can be run\n390: \t// in parallel with other plugins during PreBind phase.\n391: \t// The scheduler groups consecutive plugins that return AllowParallel: true\n392: \t// and runs them in parallel.\n393: \t// A plugin that returns AllowParallel: false breaks the parallel group\n394: \t// and runs sequentially.\n395: \t// Note: skipped plugins are effectively ignored, but if a skipped plugin returns\n396: \t// AllowParallel: false, it still breaks the parallel group of adjacent plugins.\n397: \tAllowParallel bool\n398: }\n399: \n400: // Plugin is the parent type for all the scheduling framework plugins.\n401: type Plugin interface {\n402: \tName() string\n403: }\n404: \n405: // PreEnqueuePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreEnqueue\" plugins.\n406: // These plugins are called prior to adding Pods to activeQ or backoffQ.\n407: // Note: an preEnqueue plugin is expected to be lightweight and efficient, so it's not expected to\n408: // involve expensive calls like accessing external endpoints; otherwise it'd block other\n409: // Pods' enqueuing in event handlers.\n410: type PreEnqueuePlugin interface {\n411: \tPlugin\n412: \t// PreEnqueue is called prior to adding Pods to activeQ or backoffQ.\n413: \tPreEnqueue(ctx context.Context, p *v1.Pod) *Status\n414: }\n415: \n416: // LessFunc is the function to sort pod info\n417: type LessFunc func(podInfo1, podInfo2 QueuedPodInfo) bool\n418: \n419: // QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"QueueSort\" plugins.\n420: // These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\n421: // plugin may be enabled at a time.\n422: type QueueSortPlugin interface {\n423: \tPlugin\n424: \t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\n425: \tLess(QueuedPodInfo, QueuedPodInfo) bool\n426: }\n427: \n428: // EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\n429: // move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\n430: // In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\n431: // and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\n432: // Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\n433: // and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\n434: // This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\n435: // and we have no choose but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\n436: //\n437: // Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) must implement this interface,\n438: // otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\n439: //\n440: // Also, if EventsToRegister returns an empty list, that means the Pods failed by the plugin are not requeued by any events,\n441: // which doesn't make sense in most cases (very likely misuse)\n442: // since the pods rejected by the plugin could be stuck in the unschedulable pod pool forever.\n443: //\n444: // If plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\n445: type EnqueueExtensions interface {\n446: \tPlugin\n447: \t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\n448: \t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\n449: \t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n450: \t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\n451: \t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\n452: \t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\n453: \t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\n454: \t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\n455: \t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\n456: \t//\n457: \t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\n458: \tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\n459: }\n460: \n461: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\n462: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\n463: // state.\n464: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\n465: \t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n466: \t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n467: \tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd PodInfo, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\n468: \t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n469: \t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n470: \tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove PodInfo, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\n471: }\n472: \n473: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreFilter\" plugins.\n474: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. Plugins that implement PreFilterPlugin should\n475: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\n476: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\n477: \tPlugin\n478: \t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\n479: \t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n480: \t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n481: \t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n482: \t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n483: \t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n484: \t//\n485: \t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n486: \t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n487: \tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodes []NodeInfo) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n488: \t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n489: \t// or nil if it does not. A Pre-filter plugin can provide extensions to incrementally\n490: \t// modify its pre-processed info. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n491: \t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n492: \t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n493: \t// Filter again on a specific node.\n494: \tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n495: }\n496: \n497: // FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n498: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n499: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n500: // These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n501: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n502: // Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n503: // running the pod. Plugins that implement FilterPlugin should\n504: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\n505: type FilterPlugin interface {\n506: \tPlugin\n507: \t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n508: \t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n509: \t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n510: \t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n511: \t//\n512: \t// \"Error\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\n513: \t//\n514: \t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n515: \t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n516: \t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n517: \t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n518: \t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n519: \t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n520: \t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n521: \t//\n522: \t// Plugins are encouraged to check the context for cancellation.\n523: \t// Once canceled, they should return as soon as possible with\n524: \t// an UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status that includes the\n525: \t// `context.Cause(ctx)` error explanation. For example, the\n526: \t// context gets canceled when a sufficient number of suitable\n527: \t// nodes have been found and searching for more isn't necessary\n528: \t// anymore.\n529: \tFilter(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\n530: }\n531: \n532: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n533: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n534: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n535: \tPlugin\n536: \t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n537: \t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n538: \t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\n539: \t//\n540: \t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\n541: \t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n542: \t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n543: \t//\n544: \t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n545: \t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n546: \t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n547: \t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n548: \t//\n549: \t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n550: \t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\n551: \t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\n552: \t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\n553: \tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusReader) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n554: }\n555: \n556: // PreScorePlugin is an interface for \"PreScore\" plugin. PreScore is an\n557: // informational extension point. Plugins will be called with a list of nodes\n558: // that passed the filtering phase. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n559: // state or to generate logs/metrics. Plugins that implement PreScorePlugin should\n560: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\n561: type PreScorePlugin interface {\n562: \tPlugin\n563: \t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n564: \t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\n565: \t// the pod will be rejected\n566: \t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\n567: \t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n568: \tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []NodeInfo) *Status\n569: }\n570: \n571: // ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\n572: type ScoreExtensions interface {\n573: \t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \"Score\"\n574: \t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\n575: \t// a success status.\n576: \tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\n577: }\n578: \n579: // ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Score\" plugins to rank\n580: // nodes that passed the filtering phase. Plugins that implement ScorePlugin should\n581: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\n582: type ScorePlugin interface {\n583: \tPlugin\n584: \t// Score is called on each filtered node. It must return success and an integer\n585: \t// indicating the rank of the node. All scoring plugins must return success or\n586: \t// the pod will be rejected.\n587: \tScore(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeInfo NodeInfo) (int64, *Status)\n588: \n589: \t// ScoreExtensions returns a ScoreExtensions interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\n590: \tScoreExtensions() ScoreExtensions\n591: }\n592: \n593: // ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\n594: // methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\n595: // used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\n596: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\n597: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\n598: // rejection of the pod.\n599: type ReservePlugin interface {\n600: \tPlugin\n601: \t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\n602: \t// updated. If this method returns a failed Status, the scheduler will call\n603: \t// the Unreserve method for all enabled ReservePlugins.\n604: \tReserve(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n605: \t// Unreserve is called by the scheduling framework when a reserved pod was\n606: \t// rejected, an error occurred during reservation of subsequent plugins, or\n607: \t// in a later phase. The Unreserve method implementation must be idempotent\n608: \t// and may be called by the scheduler even if the corresponding Reserve\n609: \t// method for the same plugin was not called.\n610: \tUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n611: }\n612: \n613: // PreBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreBind\" plugins.\n614: // These plugins are called before a pod being scheduled.\n615: type PreBindPlugin interface {\n616: \tPlugin\n617: \t// PreBindPreFlight is called before PreBind, and the plugin is supposed to return two values:\n618: \t// - PreBindPreFlightResult (nil is valid, and means results with the zero values on all fields).\n619: \t// - Success, Skip, or Error status.\n620: \t// If it returns Success, it means this PreBind plugin will handle this pod.\n621: \t// If it returns Skip, it means this PreBind plugin has nothing to do with the pod, and PreBind will be skipped.\n622: \t// This function should be lightweight, and shouldn't do any actual operation, e.g., creating a volume etc.\n623: \tPreBindPreFlight(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*PreBindPreFlightResult, *Status)\n624: \n625: \t// PreBind is called before binding a pod. All prebind plugins must return\n626: \t// success or the pod will be rejected and won't be sent for binding.\n627: \tPreBind(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n628: }\n629: \n630: // PostBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PostBind\" plugins.\n631: // These plugins are called after a pod is successfully bound to a node.\n632: type PostBindPlugin interface {\n633: \tPlugin\n634: \t// PostBind is called after a pod is successfully bound. These plugins are\n635: \t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\n636: \t// up. If a plugin needs to clean-up its state after a pod is scheduled and\n637: \t// bound, PostBind is the extension point that it should register.\n638: \tPostBind(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n639: }\n640: \n641: // PermitPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Permit\" plugins.\n642: // These plugins are called before a pod is bound to a node.\n643: type PermitPlugin interface {\n644: \tPlugin\n645: \t// Permit is called before binding a pod (and before prebind plugins). Permit\n646: \t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\n647: \t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\n648: \t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\n649: \t// waiting. Bind\n655: // plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\n656: type BindPlugin interface {\n657: \tPlugin\n658: \t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\n659: \t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\n660: \t// or not to handle the given Pod. The sign fragments from all plugins are combined\n668: // together to create a unified signature.\n669: type SignFragment struct {\n670: \t// Pod signature fragments are identified by a key, i.e., fragments with the same key\n671: \t// should contain the same value for the same pod. Plugin authors can return the same SignFragment\n672: \t// from multiple plugins, the framework just ignores duplicates. This allows plugins to share signers easily.\n673: \t//\n674: \t// Fragment names can be found in k8s.io/kube-scheduler/framework/signers.go. New fragment names for\n675: \t// in-tree plugins should be added there, and custom plugins can also use them.\n676: \t// Simple SignFragments which return a field should have names that follow the field name they return.\n677: \t// So a SignFragment that returns NodeName would have the key:\n678: \t//\n679: \t//\t\"v1.Pod.Spec.NodeName\"\n680: \t//\n681: \t// If a SignFragment does some processing on the resource, its name should include the path to the base of the state it uses,\n682: \t// and then suffix this with a descriptive function name followed by (). (KEP-5598).\n707: \t//\n708: \t// The sign fragments from all the plugins are combined to create a single signature. Only one fragment\n709: \t// with a given key will be included.\n710: \t//\n711: \t// Status means:\n712: \t//   - Success: the signer can sign the pod, accompanied by a set of signature fragments to be included.\n713: \t//   - Unschedulable: the signer refuses to sign the pod, meaning the pod is not eligible for opportunistic batching optimization.\n714: \t//   - Error: the signer hits something _unexpected_ and cannot build sign(s). \\t\\\"k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/scheduler/apis/config\\\"\\n29: )\\n30: \\n31: // NodeToStatus contains the statuses of the Nodes where the incoming Pod was not schedulable.\\n32: type NodeToStatus struct {\\n33: \\t// nodeToStatus contains specific statuses of the nodes.\\n34: \\tnodeToStatus map[string]*fwk.Status\\n35: \\t// absentNodesStatus defines a status for all nodes that are absent in nodeToStatus map.\\n36: \\t// By default, all absent nodes are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n37: \\tabsentNodesStatus *fwk.Status\\n38: }\\n39: \\n40: // NewDefaultNodeToStatus creates NodeToStatus without any node in the map.\\n41: // The absentNodesStatus is set by default to UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n42: func NewDefaultNodeToStatus() *NodeToStatus {\\n43: \\treturn NewNodeToStatus(make(map[string]*fwk.Status), fwk.NewStatus(fwk.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable))\\n44: }\\n45: \\n46: // NewNodeToStatus creates NodeToStatus initialized with given nodeToStatus and absentNodesStatus.\\n47: func NewNodeToStatus(nodeToStatus map[string]*fwk.Status, absentNodesStatus *fwk.Status) *NodeToStatus {\\n48: \\treturn &NodeToStatus{\\n49: \\t\\tnodeToStatus:      nodeToStatus,\\n50: \\t\\tabsentNodesStatus: absentNodesStatus,\\n51: \\t}\\n52: }\\n53: \\n54: // Get returns the status for given nodeName. If the node is not in the map, the absentNodesStatus is returned.\\n55: func (m *NodeToStatus) Get(nodeName string) *fwk.Status {\\n56: \\tif status, ok := m.nodeToStatus[nodeName]; ok {\\n57: \\t\\treturn status\\n58: \\t}\\n59: \\treturn m.absentNodesStatus\\n60: }\\n61: \\n62: // Set sets status for given nodeName.\\n63: func (m *NodeToStatus) Set(nodeName string, status *fwk.Status) {\\n64: \\tm.nodeToStatus[nodeName] = status\\n65: }\\n66: \\n67: // Len returns length of nodeToStatus map. It is not aware of number of absent nodes.\\n68: func (m *NodeToStatus) Len() int {\\n69: \\treturn len(m.nodeToStatus)\\n70: }\\n71: \\n72: // AbsentNodesStatus returns absentNodesStatus value.\\n73: func (m *NodeToStatus) AbsentNodesStatus() *fwk.Status {\\n74: \\treturn m.absentNodesStatus\\n75: }\\n76: \\n77: // SetAbsentNodesStatus sets absentNodesStatus value.\\n78: func (m *NodeToStatus) SetAbsentNodesStatus(status *fwk.Status) {\\n79: \\tm.absentNodesStatus = status\\n80: }\\n81: \\n82: // ForEachExplicitNode runs fn for each node which status is explicitly set.\\n83: // Imporatant When specified, the list of plugins for\\n134: // a particular extension point are the only ones enabled. If an extension point is\\n135: // omitted from the config, then the default set of plugins is used for that extension point.\\n136: // Enabled plugins are called in the order specified here, after default plugins. If they need to\\n137: // be invoked before default plugins, default plugins must be disabled and re-enabled here in desired order.\\n138: type Plugins struct {\\n139: \\t// PreEnqueue is a list of plugins that should be invoked before adding pods to the scheduling queue.\\n140: \\tPreEnqueue PluginSet\\n141: \\n142: \\t// QueueSort is a list of plugins that should be invoked when sorting pods in the scheduling queue.\\n143: \\tQueueSort PluginSet\\n144: \\n145: \\t// PreFilter is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \\\"PreFilter\\\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\\n146: \\tPreFilter PluginSet\\n147: \\n148: \\t// Filter is a list of plugins that should be invoked when filtering out nodes that cannot run the Pod.\\n149: \\tFilter PluginSet\\n150: \\n151: \\t// PostFilter is a list of plugins that are invoked after filtering phase, but only when no feasible nodes were found for the pod.\\n152: \\tPostFilter PluginSet\\n153: \\n154: \\t// PreScore is a list of plugins that are invoked before scoring.\\n155: \\tPreScore PluginSet\\n156: \\n157: \\t// Score is a list of plugins that should be invoked when ranking nodes that have passed the filtering phase.\\n158: \\tScore PluginSet\\n159: \\n160: \\t// Reserve is a list of plugins invoked when reserving/unreserving resources\\n161: \\t// after a node is assigned to run the pod.\\n162: \\tReserve PluginSet\\n163: \\n164: \\t// Permit is a list of plugins that control binding of a Pod. These plugins can prevent or delay binding of a Pod.\\n165: \\tPermit PluginSet\\n166: \\n167: \\t// PreBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked before a pod is bound.\\n168: \\tPreBind PluginSet\\n169: \\n170: \\t// Bind is a list of plugins that should be invoked at \\\"Bind\\\" extension point of the scheduling framework.\\n171: \\t// The scheduler call these plugins in order. Scheduler skips the rest of these plugins as soon as one returns success.\\n172: \\tBind PluginSet\\n173: \\n174: \\t// PostBind is a list of plugins that should be invoked after a pod is successfully bound.\\n175: \\tPostBind PluginSet\\n176: \\n177: \\t// MultiPoint is a simplified config field for enabling plugins for all valid extension points\\n178: \\tMultiPoint PluginSet\\n179: }\\n180: \\n181: // PluginSet specifies enabled and disabled plugins for an extension point.\\n182: // If an array is empty, missing, or nil, default plugins at that extension point will be used.\\n183: type PluginSet struct {\\n184: \\t// Enabled specifies plugins that should be enabled in addition to default plugins.\\n185: \\t// These are called after default plugins and in the same order specified here.\\n186: \\tEnabled []Plugin\\n187: \\t// Disabled specifies default plugins that should be disabled.\\n188: \\t// When all default plugins need to be disabled, an array containing only one \\\"*\\\" should be provided.\\n189: \\tDisabled []Plugin\\n190: }\\n191: \\n192: // Plugin specifies a plugin name and its weight when applicable. serves as the public API. These extension points are: PreFilter (PreFilterPlugin), Filter (FilterPlugin), PostFilter (PostFilterPlugin), PreScore (PreScorePlugin), Score (ScorePlugin), Reserve (ReservePlugin), PreBind (PreBindPlugin), Bind (BindPlugin), and PostBind (PostBindPlugin). All these interfaces embed the base Plugin interface which requires a Name() method. Supporting interfaces include PreFilterExtensions (for incremental AddPod/RemovePod operations), ScoreExtensions (for NormalizeScore operations), EnqueueExtensions (for efficient pod queue management), and SignPlugin (for batching optimizations). The framework implementation is in pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go, which contains the frameworkImpl struct that maintains plugin slices for each extension point and provides Run* methods to execute them: RunPreFilterPlugins, RunFilterPlugins, RunPreScorePlugins, RunScorePlugins, RunReservePluginsReserve/Unreserve, RunPermitPlugins, RunPreBindPlugins, RunPreBindPreFlights, RunBindPlugins, and RunPostBindPlugins. The extensionPoint struct in framework.go groups plugin configuration and implementation slices, while getExtensionPoints method returns all nine extension points in order.
